  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_920b186f-da36-48cc-b9fd-5dd5ffae07a5'
      });
    }

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_107366435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107366435" />
    <a title="Ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2927182-ellen"><img alt="Ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500520747p2/2927182.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107366435?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen" href="/user/show/2927182-ellen">Ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107366435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1673220660791145831"><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1276704910p8/122081.jpg' width='300' height='400' alt='Godot' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Over the years, I've received student papers so awful, I'm tempted to just write, "Nice font choice" and move on. For Trussoni's sad book, my comment is "Nice cover." Fetching, isn't it?<br/><br/>However, what a surprise.<br/><br/>Not one of my GR friends has any mention of this book - not a review, not a to-be-read, and definitely not a wishlist pick. <br/><br/>Gee. I wonder why. <br/><br/>Several reasons come to mind. Overall, the book is a half-witted concoction clearly written in the hopes that it would become a movie, or rather t</span>
  <span id="freeText1673220660791145831" style="display:none"><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1276704910p8/122081.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="Godot" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Over the years, I've received student papers so awful, I'm tempted to just write, "Nice font choice" and move on. For Trussoni's sad book, my comment is "Nice cover." Fetching, isn't it?<br><br>However, what a surprise.<br><br>Not one of my GR friends has any mention of this book - not a review, not a to-be-read, and definitely not a wishlist pick. <br><br>Gee. I wonder why. <br><br>Several reasons come to mind. Overall, the book is a half-witted concoction clearly written in the hopes that it would become a movie, or rather the first in a series of movies, given that the book's end signals a sequel. <br><br>The Nephilim or fallen angels, who live in the midst of a somewhat Victorian-feeling society, apparently elude the notice of most mortals, despite their immense power and influence. Just how this is possible is not explained nor is angelology, which could have been somewhat fascinating, if pursued in any depth.<br><br>And, just as Maureen Dowd coined the term baldenfreude for men losing their locks, we could probably use the term wingenfreude to describe the loss of wing breadth, luster, and thickness that some of the angels are experiencing. And if the dilemma of Percival, the key male angel, sounds a bit phallic, it should. The description of Percival's former wings in contrast to his mother's flawless appendages is rife with envy and Freudian implications:<br><blockquote>His mother's wings were gorgeous, shimmering, healthy, full-plumed. A gradation of soft color radiated from the tips, where the feathers were tiny and roseate, and moved to the center of her back, where the feathers grew large and glittering. Percival's wings, when he'd had them, had been even larger than his mother's, sharp and dramatic, the feathers precisely shaped daggers of brilliant, powdery gold."</blockquote><br>Though a major character, Percival, our emasculated and evil angel, is not the main character. That spot is reserved for Sister Evangeline, a remarkably flat and undeveloped character, whose destiny is evident by perhaps page 10 or so of this 458-page book.<br><br>The only remotely compelling sections were those in Bulgaria, particularly concerning Celestine and Gabrielle. Just why in the hell I read this whole godawful mess can only be explained by major funkdom, when I read continuously (including some awful literature) and eat a lot of bubba-mycin (chicken soup).<br><br>Please view this review as a public service message. Save yourself from this book and its likely incarnation as a movie (imdb.com indicates that it's in development). aaargh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1673220660791145831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_93127826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93127826" />
    <a title="unknown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown"><img alt="unknown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579703867p2/2863914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93127826?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="unknown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="unknown" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown">unknown</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People I don't like</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to unknown by: </span>
      The stupid New York Times
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=52-in-2010">52-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=worst-reads">worst-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=zzzz">zzzz</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93127826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14704677429563985884">This one kept losing stars as it went. The broad concept was really interesting, excerpting one of those weird bits of the bible and making it the basis for an otherworldly, fantastical story. But the characters are flat and the writing is dull -- most of the first half of the book is scenes of people doing research, and we get to read right along with them as they examine ancient historical texts and first-hand accounts of angelic encounters. This is about as exciting as reading a musty old his</span>
  <span id="freeText14704677429563985884" style="display:none">This one kept losing stars as it went. The broad concept was really interesting, excerpting one of those weird bits of the bible and making it the basis for an otherworldly, fantastical story. But the characters are flat and the writing is dull -- most of the first half of the book is scenes of people doing research, and we get to read right along with them as they examine ancient historical texts and first-hand accounts of angelic encounters. This is about as exciting as reading a musty old history textbook can be, but leaves you ready for some action.<br /><br />Sadly, when the action finally does start up, the book quickly falls apart. Danielle Trussoni clearly has zero skill in writing a thriller, and the frantic final third grows increasingly ludicrous and difficult to follow, with several poorly-staged battles between demonic creatures and old nuns and an anticlimactic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/968.The_Da_Vinci_Code__Robert_Langdon___2_" title="The Da Vinci Code (Robert Langdon, #2) by Dan Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">The Da Vinci Code</a> search for a hidden historical object that is simply there to pad out the story needlessly. The writing is very sloppy and many confrontations don't make much sense (at one point the villain has a gun trained on the heroes but neglects to use it for no discernible reason, even as one of them <i>slowly assembles a mysterious object that might spell the villain's defeat</i>).<br /><br />The ending springs a Star Wars-esque moral choice on the lead character pretty much out of nowhere and the book ends on a very sour note, clearly setting things up for a sequel that I would guess perhaps 10 percent of those who slog all the way through Angelology will actually bother to read.<br /><br />Oh, and it's going to be made into a doubtlessly terrible movie. Hooray.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14704677429563985884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94222796" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94222796" />
    <a title="Kevin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2240181-kevin"><img alt="Kevin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374702578p2/2240181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94222796?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/2240181-kevin">Kevin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94222796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5914223926808747401">Honestly, if I could give it 3.5 stars, I would. Since I can't, I'm rounding up, as a gesture towards giving the author the benefit of the doubt, expecting that the next book will be better.<br/><br/>Angelology is a mixed bag. Personally, I find angel lore, and other mythologies, fascinating, and I thoroughly enjoyed the mix of Judeo-Christian and Greek myth, Talmudic scholarship and discussion of the Book of Enoch (a personal favorite). The subject of the Nephilim has intrigued me since I first read Made</span>
  <span id="freeText5914223926808747401" style="display:none">Honestly, if I could give it 3.5 stars, I would. Since I can't, I'm rounding up, as a gesture towards giving the author the benefit of the doubt, expecting that the next book will be better.<br /><br />Angelology is a mixed bag. Personally, I find angel lore, and other mythologies, fascinating, and I thoroughly enjoyed the mix of Judeo-Christian and Greek myth, Talmudic scholarship and discussion of the Book of Enoch (a personal favorite). The subject of the Nephilim has intrigued me since I first read Madeline L'Engle as a kid. So . . . A+ on an interesting new take on very intriguing subject matter.<br /><br />I understand this is the Ms. Trussoni's first novel, her first book being a solidly non-fiction memoir. I believe that this is apparent in her writing style. Frankly, I found the narrative voice to be rather dry for a work of fiction, especially one of the fantastic variety, but perfectly in keeping, however, with the expected tone of a diarist. It is also quite telling that the most compelling part of the book was the section detailing the personal memories of a young woman's life and education in WWII-era France. It was written in the first person, and the character, Celestine, was by far the most well-developed, and most distinctive voice in the entire novel. Clearly Ms. Trussoni is more comfortable, at least at the moment, with this style of narration. <br /><br />The other characters in the book suffered somewhat from a lack of differentiation of voice; they all ran together and "read" quite similarly, from evil Nephilim to nuns, to aged angelologists. This was something of an unfortunate impediment when trying to identify with the various characters, and I hope that further work in fiction will help Ms. Trussoni better develop individual character voice.<br /><br /><br />The author is, however, quite skilled in description and her world was very easy to visualize, often vividly so. Unfortunately, her adeptness in this area overbalanced her lesser abilities in characterization and resulted in large sections of the book feeling overly expository, which was surprising, because the book had some truly exciting action bits.<br /><br />Despite the book's flaws, however, Ms. Trussoni really did succeed in drawing me in, particularly after the aforementioned very engaging second section of the book, and left me looking forward to the next novel in the series. She is clearly a skilled and talented author, and I expect that she will quickly develop better fictional narrative skills. While I don't believe the book is quite worth the hype, it is still well worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5914223926808747401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18360677213661871176">Well...the cover is FABULOUS.<br/><br/>Ok guys, I will admit it: I don't like nuns. I mean, not on a PERSONAL level, but their world view is not compelling in a general fictional sense, and they've always bugged me since one of my first acting classes when I had to play Agnes of God in a scene, and I remember I spilled Coke on myself during the performance and broke character and got yelled at. So this could be my personal problem with one of the main characters that is skewing my opinion. Because she's a</span>
  <span id="freeText18360677213661871176" style="display:none">Well...the cover is FABULOUS.<br /><br />Ok guys, I will admit it: I don't like nuns. I mean, not on a PERSONAL level, but their world view is not compelling in a general fictional sense, and they've always bugged me since one of my first acting classes when I had to play Agnes of God in a scene, and I remember I spilled Coke on myself during the performance and broke character and got yelled at. So this could be my personal problem with one of the main characters that is skewing my opinion. Because she's a nun. To be clear.<br /><br />There was just WEIRD world building in this book. I couldn't grasp onto it, nothing ever felt REAL to me, so it was hard for me to suspend disbelief. I think there was some interesting lore invented here, and some compelling characters, but it was just a bit confusing for my tastes. Probably it was the nun thing. Sally Field was so creepy to me as a kid with that outfit on too, like, she could never get in a sportscar, am I right?!<br /><br />Anyhoo, I think if you like Dan Brown's books this is JUST PERFECT for you. So there are tons of people out there who will like it. I wanted a bit more fantasy in this urban fantasy, that's all.<br /><br />Nuns, sigh.</span>

<div id="review_100292076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100292076?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143145264" href="/book/show/7705587-angelology">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100292076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16227680787055821957">I am so glad I found this on audiobook at the library. It turned out to be a very good medium for this story. I have to say that for a slow starter, I really got drawn into this book, and when it ended, I had separation anxiety!<br/><br/><b>Two things kept me from giving this a five star rating:</b><br/><br/>1. The slow, meandering start. I was initially thinking, uh-oh, this might turn out to be a real snoozer. Boy was I wrong!<br/>2. The ending was a cliffie that really got my blood pressure up! I didn't like the way this no</span>
  <span id="freeText16227680787055821957" style="display:none">I am so glad I found this on audiobook at the library. It turned out to be a very good medium for this story. I have to say that for a slow starter, I really got drawn into this book, and when it ended, I had separation anxiety!<br /><br /><b>Two things kept me from giving this a five star rating:</b><br /><br />1. The slow, meandering start. I was initially thinking, uh-oh, this might turn out to be a real snoozer. Boy was I wrong!<br />2. The ending was a cliffie that really got my blood pressure up! I didn't like the way this novel concluded at all. I hate feeling like I'm being manipulated to read the next book in a series, and it felt that way. I'd rather read a book series that has books that begin and conclude in a natural way. Some resolution, but threads that encourage me to pick up the next book. That was so not the case here. I would have kept reading anyway, but now I feel like my arm is being twisted to read the next book.<br /><br /><b>Things I loved about this book:</b><br /><br />1. The scholarly tone wouldn't work for everyone, but since I am a bookworm nerd who likes to research topics that are of interest, I could really get into the angelologists and their penchant for delving deeply into subjects in their field. And their subject knowledge.. .Wow! Most of the main characters were in one way or another scholars or people who really knew their stuff. They spent their lives reading and immersing themselves in the past. That spoke to me. <br />2. I loved the epistolary format, a significant portion of the book written as parts of journal entries and book excerpts. It was executed very well. One would think that this would make the book dry, but it didn’t.<br />3. The narrator was fantastic. She did a gorgeous French accent (and believe me, most of the book is in various French viewpoints), and she made each of the characters sound very different. With the male viewpoints, her voice was lower and conveyed a male speaking. She really brought them to life, and brought a vivid image of the story to life, and I could get an idea of what each character was like based on the way she spoke their parts.<br />4. Ms. Trussoni gets the duality of angels. They are so beautiful they are irresistible, but there are so powerful and dangerous that one never truly forgets (or shouldn’t to their regret) their celestial nature, so far above humans. And then, there are the nephilim. Oh my goodness. They were so evil! I had hopes that creatures of a once divine origin, so beautiful to look at, would have some goodness inside. Not at all! I was continually surprised at how sinister and even corrupt they were. They thought absolutely nothing about humans, or God, or their celestial origins. They were all about obtaining and keeping power on earth.<br />5. Angelology itself as the focus of this book. Who knew? Wow! It’s more than just being an angel scholar. It’s your life, and there is no sacrifice too great, as I learned as I read. It’s all for a purpose, to prepare for the battle against very powerful foes, the nephilim. The people in this avocation that we become acquaintances with in this book suffer so greatly, and as I listened, it was clear why. Their foes were such that it took all their energies to fight them, and losing one’s life could be a given at any time.<br />6. Ms. Trussoni did such a good job of tying all the various narrators together. The story spans over a thousand years (well actually goes back to biblical times), but it all plays a part, and each narrator took my attention and held it hostage as I listened.<br />7. Percival Grigori was a fascinating villain. There were times I felt really sorry for him, and other times I hated him. His highly complicated relationship with Gabriella Levy-French Valco made for some good reading! The societies that the nephilim had built and how they became the ones controlling all the power and money in the modern world felt so plausible, part of me wonders if this is truly possible. It kind of makes sense! <br /><b>Final Thoughts</b>:<br />Although the ending was a buzz kill, I was very impressed overall with this book. The angel parts were surreally intoxicating. I found I cared about the characters, and I was so engaged with their struggles. This book found my angel love and pulled me tight to the narrative. The unreal beauty of the angels, the black hearts of the nephilim, the intense struggle of the frail humans against unimaginably strong (but strangely frail in some ways) celestial creatures. But then, those angelologists have some serious tricks up their sleeve. If you are a reader who loves angels, you should add this to the reading list. <br /><br />Overall rating: <b> 4.5 celestial stars</b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16227680787055821957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_385352846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385352846" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470503541p2/11382577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385352846?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=best-paranormal-fiction">best-paranormal-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=weird-but-good">weird-but-good</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385352846" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9989132124677347689">When you read as much as I do, it is rare to come across a totally unique story. Angelology is that rare gem.<br/><br/>This book has almost every element a great book should offer: multi-faceted, fascinating characters, an exciting, complex, layered plot, and really excellent writing. The story is a tapestry of interwoven storylines, that includes history, religion, philosophy, art, puzzles, and scavenger hunts.<br/><br/>The story revolves around Sister Evangeline, a young nun, who has been part of the Franciscan S</span>
  <span id="freeText9989132124677347689" style="display:none">When you read as much as I do, it is rare to come across a totally unique story. Angelology is that rare gem.<br /><br />This book has almost every element a great book should offer: multi-faceted, fascinating characters, an exciting, complex, layered plot, and really excellent writing. The story is a tapestry of interwoven storylines, that includes history, religion, philosophy, art, puzzles, and scavenger hunts.<br /><br />The story revolves around Sister Evangeline, a young nun, who has been part of the Franciscan Sisters of Perpetual Adoration convent since the age of twelve, left there by her father after the tragic, and mysterious death of her mother.<br /><br />The Convent has a well-known archive and library with information on Angels. When an art-historian asks permission to visit and access the archives, Sister Evangeline as the nun responsible for correspondence, prepares the usual polite denial. And yet, she is intrigued by the request, which contends that Abigail Rockefellar corresponded with a previous Mother Superior of the convent.<br /><br />Curious, Evangeline searches the archives and finds a letter from Mrs. Rockefellar.<br /><br />This sets off a chain of events which show Evangeline that she is not the person she thought she was, and that her mother and grandmother were keepers of an exceptionally special calling - Angelologists, who have hunted and attempted to exterminate evil rogue angels, called Nephilim, who are living among us to this day.<br /><br />But Evangeline soon realizes that her own life may be in danger because of events set in motion hundreds of years in the past, and that she must discover the truth of her heritage.<br /><br />At the same time, Percival Grigori, son of one of the premier Nephilim families, is suffering from a debilitating crippling disease, that will kill him, unless he can unravel a mystery and obtain a cure, which he believes is being hidden by the Angelologists.<br /><br />It isn't possible to do this book real justice in a review. It has so much to offer you have to read it to appreciate it, and I recommend you do if you like thoughtful, well-written, fascinating historical fiction with a number of psychological thriller twists and turns. <br /><br />Definitely one of the best books I've ever read! This is the author's first book, and I really hope she has more stories like this one in her!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9989132124677347689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_92554667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92554667" />
    <a title="Eve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/758088-eve"><img alt="Eve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491192188p2/758088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92554667?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eve" href="/user/show/758088-eve">Eve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92554667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11046828130143387402">Dare I say it? Yes, I dare say - <br/>Angelology by Danielle Trussoni is the heir to Elizabeth Kostova's The Historian. <br/><br/>Angelology is a breathtaking story of ambitious scope: good vs. evil, man vs. fallen angels, Nazis, Greek mythology, the Bible, Milton (Angelology owes much to Paradise Lost). And the heroine is a nun - gotta love it! <br/><br/>Sister Evangeline is leading a quiet life of prayer in a convent situated in Milton, New York, when she receives a letter from Paul Verlaine asking for access to the c</span>
  <span id="freeText11046828130143387402" style="display:none">Dare I say it? Yes, I dare say - <br />Angelology by Danielle Trussoni is the heir to Elizabeth Kostova's The Historian. <br /><br />Angelology is a breathtaking story of ambitious scope: good vs. evil, man vs. fallen angels, Nazis, Greek mythology, the Bible, Milton (Angelology owes much to Paradise Lost). And the heroine is a nun - gotta love it! <br /><br />Sister Evangeline is leading a quiet life of prayer in a convent situated in Milton, New York, when she receives a letter from Paul Verlaine asking for access to the convent's archives. With this one request, Evangeline and Verlaine set off a dangerous chain of events that are connected to the secret society of Angelologists, those who have made it their lives' work to study and defeat humankind's oldest enemy - the fallen angels. <br /><br />The Society of Angelologists go back many generations, claiming as its members, Sir Thomas Aquinas, Roger Bacon, Milton, of course. They are scholars of theology, scientists, men and women of the cloth who throughout the years have waged a secret war against the Nephilim, the evil offspring of the fallen angels who pass as humans. The darkest periods of human history, such as the Inquisition and the Nazis' rise to power, are attributed to the machinations of the half-human, half-angel Nephilim. However, some of the Nephilim are falling prey to a degenerative disease, and they have become desperate to find a cure. <br /><br />For many years now, the Angelologists and Nephilim alike have been searching for a hidden, fabled treasure from the Archangel Michael himself, which, if the Nephilim were to obtain it would be their instrument to unlimited power on earth and also cure their mysterious wasting disease. Within the forgotten archives of Sister Evangeline's convent lies the key to its location. From Bulgaria, to Paris, to New York - the Angelologists race to find this precious artifact before the Nephilim. <br /><br />Angelology started off slowly, as it opens with details of the uneventful, meditative life of a nun; however, once it hits the Angelology part, it just takes off and soars. Much like Lucifer in Paradise Lost, the Nephilim are mesmerizing figures, more so than the human characters in Angelology. The vivid passages describing them leap off the page.<br /><br /><i>The angelologists examined the body. It was intact, without decay, the skin as smooth and as white as parchment. The lifeless aquamarine eyes gazed heavenward. Pale curls fell against a high forehead and sculptural shoulders, forming a halo of golden hair... It should not have surprised them to find the angel in that preserved condition. The fingernails, nacreous as the inside of an oyster shell; the long, smooth, navel-less stomach; the eerie translucency of the skin---everything about the creature was as they knew it would be, even the positioning of the wings was correct. And yet it was too lovely, too vital for something they had studied only in airless libraries... <br /><br />All their professional lives they had waited to see it. Although not one of them would have admitted so, they secretly suspected to find a monstrous corpse, all bones and fiber shreds, like something unearthed from an archeological dig. Instead there was this: a delicate tapering hand, an aquiline nose, pink lips in a frozen kiss. The angelologists hovered above the body, gazing down in anticipation, as if they expected the creature to blink its eyes and wake.</i><br /><br />As diabolical and soulless as they are, the fallen angels are seductive; I would love to have majored in Angelology! I love that all the Angelologists have angelic names: Seraphina, Gabriella, Raphael, Celestine, Angela, Evangeline. To give Angelology a scholarly feel, Trussoni weaves Biblical passages, letters, journals, and historic-esque accounts within the fantastical plot (hence the comparison with The Historian). <br /><br />I just could not stop reading this book and raced without break to the thrilling yet unexpected ending. <br /><br />I'm further excited to find out that there's a planned sequel (the ending certainly begs for it) called Angelopolis. I hope Trussoni finishes that one soon!<br /><br />My enthusiasm for Angelology has me wondering - Are angels are the new vampires???<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11046828130143387402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_191834819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191834819" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3095901-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522768835p2/3095901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191834819?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/3095901-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3095901-karen?shelf=ladywritten">ladywritten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3095901-karen?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3095901-karen?shelf=specfic">specfic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191834819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17304701593548014030">All 452 pages of it. Yup.<br/><br/>I had issues with this book from the first page. The writing is...not good. I know Trussoni went to Iowa (which is usually a yardstick of some kind) and she wrote an acclaimed memoir before this, and this very book is a NY Times Notable Book of 2010. So you'd think she'd write a good sentence. But no. The book is full to bursting with things like: <br/><br/>"Verlaine stared at her, flabbergasted at what this otherwise rational woman had just said."<br/><br/>and: <br/><br/>"The chaos of people sloggin</span>
  <span id="freeText17304701593548014030" style="display:none">All 452 pages of it. Yup.<br /><br />I had issues with this book from the first page. The writing is...not good. I know Trussoni went to Iowa (which is usually a yardstick of some kind) and she wrote an acclaimed memoir before this, and this very book is a NY Times Notable Book of 2010. So you'd think she'd write a good sentence. But no. The book is full to bursting with things like: <br /><br />"Verlaine stared at her, flabbergasted at what this otherwise rational woman had just said."<br /><br />and: <br /><br />"The chaos of people slogging through the slush, the squish of buildings, the incessant movement of traffic in every direction--New York City was deeply familiar, despite her years away."<br /><br />The squish of buildings?<br /><br />So, overall the book feels rushed and superficial. It's also about 100 pages too long, in part because there's so much redundant and unimportant information--and long, long passages devoted to careful reiteration of past events and their possible significance. At the same time it's missing major appendages--like believable character development, realistic motivation for a shoe-horned-in romance, thoughtful description of many places people &amp; things...<br /><br />I made myself read to the end of this one because I'm interested in literary writers who turn their hand to genre. Sometimes this can go very well (Michael Chabon, Alden Bell) and sometimes it goes very badly (Justin Cronin, Danielle Trussoni.) I think the secret to writing good genre fiction is not assuming your readers are simple-minded, and not treating it like a cash cow for the movie rights. Where I think both Cronin and Trussoni <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angelology_%28novel%29#Publishing_and_film_interest" rel="nofollow noopener">did very well</a>. <br /><br />So hey, this could be a really long, overwrought movie at a theater near you soon! <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17304701593548014030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104785392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104785392" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2042383-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601591210p2/2042383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104785392?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/2042383-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104785392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3795911649524856855">Gah...I wanted to like this book so much. Its premise is so fascinating, but it's execution is like being trapped in a coffin with a rich, old dead woman (one who is wearing enough perfume to clear a street riot) and having to listen to her talk about her less-than-exciting life as a nun.<br/><br/>You know there are some exciting parts somewhere if only she'd stop blathering on about the absolute stupidest details, like the color of the typewriter she used to respond to some man's letter or the size of th</span>
  <span id="freeText3795911649524856855" style="display:none">Gah...I wanted to like this book so much. Its premise is so fascinating, but it's execution is like being trapped in a coffin with a rich, old dead woman (one who is wearing enough perfume to clear a street riot) and having to listen to her talk about her less-than-exciting life as a nun.<br /><br />You know there are some exciting parts somewhere if only she'd stop blathering on about the absolute stupidest details, like the color of the typewriter she used to respond to some man's letter or the size of the flowers on a small pink cake she ate when she was seven.<br /><br />I got halfway through before I got smart enough to claw my way back to the land of the living...<br /><br />Stephen King wrote that description is like helping someone out of quicksand. You should throw them a rope, something they can hold easily, not 200 lbs. of steel cable.<br /><br />I think Danielle was trying to balance out the fantastical (angels, etc.) with the every day. Her version of the every day was 200 lbs. of steel cable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3795911649524856855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1738729158?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1256603-sara">Sara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1738729158" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12883382078389934363">Prologue: In which I apologize to the people who like this book<br/><br/>I'd like to apologize for what you're about to read. I know you really enjoyed this and you thought it was just an amazing fantasy epic on par with say Dan Brown's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/968.The_Da_Vinci_Code__Robert_Langdon___2_' title='The Da Vinci Code (Robert Langdon, #2) by Dan Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Da Vinci Code</a>. <br/><br/>Me? I should have known better then to read a book that had words like "if you loved <i>The Da Vinci Code</i>" on the back cover. My feelings about <i>The Da Vinci Code</i> and Dan Brown cannot be fully expressed in words but it’s very difficult to spell out primal sc</span>
  <span id="freeText12883382078389934363" style="display:none">Prologue: In which I apologize to the people who like this book<br /><br />I'd like to apologize for what you're about to read. I know you really enjoyed this and you thought it was just an amazing fantasy epic on par with say Dan Brown's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/968.The_Da_Vinci_Code__Robert_Langdon___2_" title="The Da Vinci Code (Robert Langdon, #2) by Dan Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">The Da Vinci Code</a>. <br /><br />Me? I should have known better then to read a book that had words like "if you loved <i>The Da Vinci Code</i>" on the back cover. My feelings about <i>The Da Vinci Code</i> and Dan Brown cannot be fully expressed in words but it’s very difficult to spell out primal screams of rage so you'll just have to imagine that's what I'm doing right now.<br /><br />So I thought I'd have a little fun with this review (you will note I have hidden it all under a spoiler tag because of well spoilers but also because no one likes seeing something they loved torn to shreds and occasionally I'm not a totally horrible person). <br /><br />Now without further ado I present my views on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6691426.Angelology__Angelology___1_" title="Angelology (Angelology, #1) by Danielle Trussoni" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelology</a>...<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dear Prospective Angelologist:<br /><br />Congratulations! By developing a completely random interest in angels you’ve taken the first step toward membership in an exclusive and super secret group of people just like you that’s been around for thousands of years (we’re not sure of the exact date because our records and research are a disorganized mess that we don’t understand AT ALL)! I mean yeah there are thousands of us all over the world and we have elaborate, architecturally astounding, amazingly decorated schools everywhere (please see the attached 200 pages for full descriptions of our Montparnasse school where very long, utterly pointless flashbacks will be taking place for hundreds of pages) but we’re totally super secret! Shhhhhhhhhhhh no one knows!!!!<br /><br />The first thing you need to know is bad Angels and human women used to do the nasty. Other Angels put those bad Angels in an easily accessible prison in a cavern under some mountains but don’t worry because for some reason no one can find it even though it’s right outside a well populated town where people have gone for hundreds upon hundreds of years to listen to the Angels singing and lots of people know about it. The bad Angels are totally hidden in their prison. Totally. For sure. There’s also a magical harp down there that everryyybbbooodddyyyy wants. Because it’s a magical harp that’s magical!<br /><br />The resulting children of humans and Angels are called Nephalim and they are the woooorrrsssttttt. They’re super pretty, super rich, and totally, totally evil. No one knows about them except for the thousands of people they employ, work with and hang out with. Oh how are they evil? Examples? <br /><br />Um.<br /><br />Hang on a minute….<br /><br />No seriously just wait for a second…<br /><br />Okay we don’t have any <i>examples</i> per se but they’re always around whenever bad stuff happens and then they conveniently disappear before they can get caught. It’s all their fault that organized society is like a thing! Before Nephalim we were happy, ignorant, cave people who were totally innocent and then the Angels taught the Nephalim about stuff like reading and making medicine and fire. Totally evil right!? Right!? And and and they are super, SUPER lazy. Like they wait for us to do all the research on the magical harp that is magical and then they STEAL it! Because they’re evil stealers!! Oh and Darwin! Did we mention Darwin!? They totally took his work and messed it up! No we don’t know what it was about before they got it but after it was about evolution! Evolution!? What kind of bullshit is that!? TOTALLY evil right!? And Nazi’s!!! They hung out with Nazis! Super super evil right!? Who likes Nazis!?<br /><br />Okay sorry, we got excited there for a minute, but they’re totally bad news. For serious. But don't tell anyone because its a SECRET!!! SHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!!!!!<br /><br />But what exactly is Angelology? We’re so glad you asked! Unfortunately we’re never going to give you an answer. What we do primarily is read about angels and have arguments about what we’re reading. Sometimes we say scary sounding things like “they must be stopped!” We’re going to say a lot of encouraging things to you like “always question the research!” and “no account of an angelogical event is ever totally accurate!” but then we’re going to totally confuse you by insisting you take everything we tell you as the gospel truth! <br /><br />Did someone say gospel!? What a perfect segway! You don’t have to be religious at all to be an Angelologist! We have members from all sorts of backgrounds one of them is even a Buddhist! But you should know that everything written in the Christian bible is the literal truth and everything that happened in it actually happened! Noah's flood? Cornerstone of our ENTIRE belief structure. Yeah, yeah we’re total hypocrites tell us something we don’t know! <br /><br />Hypocrites! Another great segway! So remember when we were all “Nephalim are bad, ohhhh they do horrible stuff agghhhhh?” So sometimes we kind of do the exact same stuff. Like lying and manipulation and stealing and murder. We maybe kind of murdered a few people... BUT we do it for the right reasons so it’s okay! Cool? Cool.<br /><br />Do you want to hear about some of our illustrious members? <br /><br />Well, first we have Evangeline Valko. She’s a nun who doesn’t really care about being a nun or God or anything. Her dad put her in a convent after Nephalim killed her mom who was doing important “angel science.” Conveniently this is the same convent were super secret things that the Nephalim would kill to get are hidden! Evangeline’s dad is super smart! Evangeline doesn’t have a frickin’ clue what is going on at any given moment. She's super confused! She’s also technically not an Angelologist and openly questions whether angels are even a thing despite knowing all about her parents’ work and having seen them in person herself. Several times. She’s not remotely compelling because literally all we can tell you about her is; she’s a nun who’s confused!<br /><br />Then there’s Verlaine. He’s a “researcher” hired by evil Nephalim to do “research” into obscure relationships between the Rockefeller’s and the convent Evangeline lives in. He LOVES art and talking about the Rockefellers. Did we mention he’s super into the Rockefellers? Cause he is. Into the Rockefellers. He loooovvveesss the Rockefellers and wants to find some letters they wrote to a nun in Evangeline’s convent. He’s also in love with Evangeline despite the fact that they’ve been in the same room together for all of five minutes total. He’s also not at all compelling because all we can tell you is; he’s a researcher who’s in love with Evangeline!<br /><br />Our favorites though are Celestine and Gabriella who you will learn all about as Celestine (who’s an old nun in Evangeline’s convent now) has an incredibly detailed dream that takes you through a second by second recap of every single solitary moment leading up to the time she went on a mission during World War II to take blood samples from a dead angel and trip over the magical harp that will somehow stop the Nephalim with its magical harpiness. <br /><br />You will be positively riveted by Celestine’s keen observations that her roommate Gabriella is “hiding something” based entirely on Gabriella’s facial expressions and style of dress. You will marvel at their “deep friendship” despite Celestine’s never ending whining about how jealous she is of every single thing about Gabriella, who to be fair is smarter, prettier, and more interesting. You will gasp in awe over the seemingly never ending descriptions of how comfortable the chairs are at Angelology School and how big the bookcases are and how drapey the drapes are! You will fall asleep listening to the narrator doing a really great lilting French accent if you are listening to this in audio format! You will be amazed that anyone let’s Celestine cross the street by herself much less entrusts her with serious world altering information or responsibilities. She is as dumb as a rock.<br /><br />You will try desperately to figure out how <i>Angelology</i> can be so goddamn long and yet have absolutely no story or characters. <br /><br />You will be on page two where nuns are staring intently at the altar in the chapel where they pray constantly and go “huh I bet the secret thing that is hidden is hidden there!” and you will be right because you have an IQ above 4!<br /><br />You will turn bleary eyed to your CD player and shout “he’s a fucking angel!” repeatedly while Celestine wonders and wonders and wonders just who Gabriella’s tall, super pale, blond, secret lover is.<br /><br />You will cave in eventually and get the actual book out of the library because if you listen to the narrator any longer you’re going to fall asleep in your car and cause an accident. <br /><br />All of this and more can be yours if you become an Angelologist today! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12883382078389934363" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_101076872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101076872" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101076872?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143118466" href="/book/show/8690988-angelology">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=mythic-fiction">mythic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=1st-in-a-series">1st-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=angelology">angelology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=religious">religious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101076872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8619834271905718920"><b>"Angelology"</b> is not a Biblical-based novel, it is an adventure in an imaginary world. It combines angels and ancient myths and interweaves them into a contemporary setting. <br/><br/>This novel is a struggle between good and evil, between Nephilim (angels of the earth) and Human beings. It is a story of magic, and struggle, and hope. We watch as Evangeline, who grew up in a convent, encounters a world and a life she never knew existed. We are introduced to that world with her, and find ourselves suspendin</span>
  <span id="freeText8619834271905718920" style="display:none"><b>"Angelology"</b> is not a Biblical-based novel, it is an adventure in an imaginary world. It combines angels and ancient myths and interweaves them into a contemporary setting. <br /><br />This novel is a struggle between good and evil, between Nephilim (angels of the earth) and Human beings. It is a story of magic, and struggle, and hope. We watch as Evangeline, who grew up in a convent, encounters a world and a life she never knew existed. We are introduced to that world with her, and find ourselves suspending our disbelief as we watch the story unfold. <br /><br />Sister Evangeline is leading a quiet life of prayer in a convent situated in Milton, New York, when she receives a letter from Paul Verlaine asking for access to the convent's archives. With this one request, Evangeline and Verlaine set off a dangerous chain of events that are connected to the secret society of Angelologists, those who have made it their lives' work to study and defeat humankind's oldest enemy -- the fallen angels. <br /><br />The Society of Angelologists go back many generations, claiming as its members, Sir Thomas Aquinas, Roger Bacon, Milton, of course. They are scholars of theology, scientists, men and women of the cloth who throughout the years have waged a secret war against the Nephilim, the evil offspring of the fallen angels who pass as humans. The darkest periods of human history, such as the Inquisition and the Nazis' rise to power, are attributed to the machinations of the half-human, half-angel Nephilim. However, some of the Nephilim are falling prey to a degenerative disease, and they have become desperate to find a cure. <br /><br />For many years now, the Angelologists and Nephilim alike have been searching for a hidden, fabled treasure from the Archangel Michael himself, which, if the Nephilim were to obtain it would be their instrument to unlimited power on earth and also cure their mysterious wasting disease. Within the forgotten archives of Sister Evangeline's convent lies the key to its location. From Bulgaria, to Paris, to New York -- the Angelologists race to find this precious artifact before the Nephilim. <br /><br />In incredible detail, Trussoni tells a believable tale, a tale that pulls you into the very center of the struggle, one that is 3/4 adventure and 1/4 fantasy. I found myself intrigued as I met the characters and watched the story weave itself together. <br /><br />The story is engaging, fast-paced, and original. The characters are intriguing, believable, and of increasing complexity as the story develops. The settings and time periods range from Paris in the 1940's, to the mountains of Bulgaria, to modern-day New York. Whether in a convent or a cave; whether seeing events through the eyes of a bewildered little girl or a prideful centuries-old Nephilim -- you feel you are there and it feels real. <br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Angelology<br /><u>Author</u> Danielle Trussoni <br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="8619834271905718920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104317371" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104317371" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2362650-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602770009p2/2362650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104317371?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/2362650-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2362650-melissa?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104317371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10963018362065829489">When my friend Deb told me she was reading a book called Angelology, and that I had to read it, too, I was skeptical. I mean, it sounded like some funky new age treatise, and secretly, I was worried about what chemicals might be misfiring in her brain. Then she began to describe the plot, and even before she gave me the book, I was hooked.<br/><br/>Imagine a world where angels walk beside us, not as mystical guardians but as immortal (or as near to it as makes little difference) preter-natural beings with</span>
  <span id="freeText10963018362065829489" style="display:none">When my friend Deb told me she was reading a book called Angelology, and that I had to read it, too, I was skeptical. I mean, it sounded like some funky new age treatise, and secretly, I was worried about what chemicals might be misfiring in her brain. Then she began to describe the plot, and even before she gave me the book, I was hooked.<br /><br />Imagine a world where angels walk beside us, not as mystical guardians but as immortal (or as near to it as makes little difference) preter-natural beings with huge mafia-esque family businesses. Oh, they’re not ‘out’ or anything – but they exist nevertheless – at least in the reality Trussoni has created.<br /><br />Enter Sister Evangeline, orphan, nun, restless soul. She’s been assigned to work in the convent library, and one day while she’s doing just that, she intercepts a letter asking for proof of a connection between her convent’s former Mother Superior and Abigail Rockefeller, yes, the Abigail Rockefeller.<br /><br />That letter sparks a romp through art, literature and history that even Dan Brown would be humbled by, replete with mystery, intrigue, faith, science, and maybe even a little magic.<br /><br />To describe the plot more would be to ruin it. Suffice to say Angelology is a gripping paranormal mystery/thriller of epic proportions.<br /><br />Goes well with a slice of angel food cake, fresh strawberries, and a perfect cappuccino.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10963018362065829489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94891110?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/582713-amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like dan brown books</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94891110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17284928576698823012">This book did not live up to the hype. It's Dan Brown with a slightly better editor. The book is split into three sections. The first section was ok. The author did a good job of introducing the families and the specific players. The second section set up the action and gave a history of what the characters were searching for. There were parts of this section that were interesting, specifically the trip to Bulgaria. The third section, was the most similar to a Dan Brown book. It was rushed: new </span>
  <span id="freeText17284928576698823012" style="display:none">This book did not live up to the hype. It's Dan Brown with a slightly better editor. The book is split into three sections. The first section was ok. The author did a good job of introducing the families and the specific players. The second section set up the action and gave a history of what the characters were searching for. There were parts of this section that were interesting, specifically the trip to Bulgaria. The third section, was the most similar to a Dan Brown book. It was rushed: new characters were introduced that did not have distinct personalities and other characters were killed off with trite last words. In addition, the ending was clearly written to indicate that there would be a sequel. Unfortunately it read like the ending to a bad superhero movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17284928576698823012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_94323472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94323472" />
    <a title="Ronda  Tutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216375-ronda-tutt"><img alt="Ronda  Tutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475858100p2/2216375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94323472?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronda  Tutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronda  Tutt" href="/user/show/2216375-ronda-tutt">Ronda  Tutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216375-ronda-tutt?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216375-ronda-tutt?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer94323472&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94323472" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15834516550512937329">It is hard to rate this story because there were parts that were very interesting and exciting, yet there were parts that were very slow where I fell a sleep.<br/><br/>I loved the story line but I didn't like how it ended to much, I was looking for a happy ending with some romance involved. This book totally left you hanging in the end so that you will find out the rest of the story in the second book.<br/><br/>there are so many things that happen in the story but I liked all the characters especially the main ones</span>
  <span id="freeText15834516550512937329" style="display:none">It is hard to rate this story because there were parts that were very interesting and exciting, yet there were parts that were very slow where I fell a sleep.<br /><br />I loved the story line but I didn't like how it ended to much, I was looking for a happy ending with some romance involved. This book totally left you hanging in the end so that you will find out the rest of the story in the second book.<br /><br />there are so many things that happen in the story but I liked all the characters especially the main ones: <br /><br /><b>Percival Grigoris III</b> - Nephilim/Angel - whos wings were once gold but now black with disease. He contacted a degenerative disorder that had been spreading through their community. Doctors predicted his wings would die spreading the disease to his muscles and he would eventually die.<br /><br /><b>Sneja Grigori</b> - Percivals mother - her wings were the pride of the family - multicolored wings that stretched over 36 ft - they were a symbol of their blood, their breeding, the predominance of their position in the community.<br /><br /><b>Evangeline</b> - Nun - Gabriella's and Percival's granddaughter - Evangeline doesn't find out that she is 1/2 Nephilim until the end of the book.<br /><br /><b>Gabriella </b>- Angelologist - double spy - Percival's lover<br /><br /><b>Verlaine </b>- Dr in Art History - worked for Percival until he found out what he was - fancied Evangeline and realizes he was in love with her at the end.<br /><br />The things that intrigued me were how these angelologist explained how these angels existed:<br /><br /><i>"We begin in the years before the Great Flood, when heaven dispatched a fleet of two hundred angels called the Watchers to monitor the activities of creation. The Chief Watcher, according to these accounts, was named Semjaza. Samjaza was beautiful and commanding, the very image of angelic bearing."<br /><br />"The angels moved among the children of Adam and Even unseen, living quietly in the shadows, hiding in mountains, taking shelter where humanity would not find them. They traveled from region to region, following the movements of men."<br /><br />One afternoon, in the era of Jared, when the Watchers were stationed on Mount Hermon, Semjaza saw a woman bathing in a lake, her brown hair twisting about her. He called the Watchers to the edge of the mountain and together the majestic beings looked upon the woman. According to numerous doctrinal sources, it was then that Semjaza suggested the Watchers choose wives from among the children of men."<br /><br />"The women took these strange creatures as their husbands and soon became pregnant. After some time children were born to the Watchers and their wives. These creatures were called Nephilim."</i><br /><br />These Nephilim were very beautiful, tall, and gifted. The Watchers taught their children many things that were kept hidden from humanity such as secrets of fire - how to kindle and keep it, how to harness it for cooking and energy; metallurgy, the art of working precious metals into bracelets, rings, and necklaces; how to make objects out of gold and gemstones, how to use dyes for cloth, how to color their eyelids with glittering minerals ground into powder, how to melt metal and fashon swords, knives, shields, breastplates, and arrowheads; how to fight, hunt, and store meat. <br /><br />They even taught their daughters how to cast spells and how to use herbs and roots in medicines; taught them the secrets of the magical arts, teaching them a system of symbols to record their spells. they taught them astrology, how tor ead portents in the constellations, knowledge of the clouds, map the course of the sun and the moon, and taught them counter spells.<br /><br />They soon had developed their own tribe and became more powerful over humanity and taking domains of land and claiming their own kingdoms and then they took men/women human on as slaves.<br /><br /><i>"As the Nephilim ruled over earth and men perished, mankind cried to heaven for help. Michael, Uriel, Raphael, and Gabriel, the archangels who had observed the Watchers from their first descent to the world, also montored the progress of the Nephilim."<br /><br />"When commanded, the archangels confronted the Watchers, surrounding them in a ring of fire. They disarmed their brothers. Once defeated, teh Watchers were shackled and transported to a remote, unpopulated cavern high in the mountains. At the lip of the abyss, their chains heavy upon them, the Watchers were ordered to descend. Throught a crevice in the earth's crust they fell, plummeting deeper and deeper until they came to rest in a prisness of darkness. From the depths they grieved for air and light and their lost freedom. Separated from heaven and earth, awaiting the day of their release, they prayed for heaven's forgiveness. They called out for their children to save them. God ignored their pleas. The Nephilim did not come."<br /><br />"The angel, Gabriel, messenger of good news, could not abide the Watchers' anguish. In a moment of pity, he threw his lyre to his fallen brothers so that they might diminish their suffering with music. Even as the lyre fell, Gabriel realized his mistake: The lyre's music was seductive and powerful. The lyre could be used to the Watchers' benefit."</i><br /><br />The story just totally amazes me how the children of the Watchers were so selfish. Knowing that god was about to flood the earth and kill all the evil within, the Nephilim searched a way to save their race.<br /><br />If you read Genesis 6 in the KJV bible, it tells the story of why god was going to flood the earth.<br /><br /><i>Genesis Chapter 6:<br />"1. And it came to pass, when men began to multiply on the face of the earth, and daughters were born unto them,<br />2. That the sons of God saw the daughters of men that they were fair; and they took them wives of all which they chose.<br />3. And the Lord said, My spirit shall not always strive with man, for that he also is flesh: yet his days shall be an hundred and twenty years.<br />4. There were giants in the earth in those days; and also after that, when the sons of God came in unto the daughters of men, and they bare children to them, the same became mighty men which were of old, me of renown.<br />5. And God saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, and that every imagination of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually.<br />6. And it repented the Lord that he had made man on the earth, and it grieved him at his heart.<br />7. And the Lord said, I will destroy man whom I have created from the face fo the earth; both man, and beast, and the creeping thing, and the fowls of the air; for it repenteth me that I have made them."</i><br /><br />Well we all know that Noah found grace in gods eyes and this part of the story really trips me up and I have to give the writer thumbs up for this part of the story.<br /><br /><i>"High in the mountains, under a ledge that sheltered them from the rain, the Nephilim stood together, begging guidance from the daughters of Semjaza and the sons of Azazel, whom they considered to be their leaders after the Watchers had been taken below the earth."<br /><br /><i>"For some days Azazel's son and Semjaza's daughter watched the comings and goings of Noah's sons. They were called Shem, Ham, and Japheth, each very different from the others. Shem, the eldest, was dark-haired and green-eyed, with elegant hands and a brilliant way of speaking; ham was darker than Shem, with large brown eyes, great strength, and good sense; japheth had fair skin, blond hair, and blue eyes, the most frail and thin of the three. While Shem and Ham did not tire as they helped their father load animals, satchels of food, and jars of water, Japheth worked slowly. Shem and Ham and Japheth had been long married, adn between them Noah had many grandchildren."<br /><br />"Semjaza's daughter saw that Japheth's appearance was close to their own and decided that this was the brother her companion should take. The Nephilim waited for many days, watching, until Noah had loaded the final animals onto the Ark. The son of Azazel stole to the great boat. Its massive shadow fell upon him, blanketing him in shadow as he called for Japheth.<br /><br />Noah's youngest leaned over the edge of the Ark, his blond curls falling into his eyes. Azazel's son summonded Japheth to accompany him away from the seashore, along a footpath that led deep into a forest. The archangels, who stood guard at the boats prow and hull, inspecting every object that entered and exited the Ark so that it fit God's dictate, paid no attention to Japheth as he left the ship and trailed the luminous stranger into the woods.<br /><br />As japheth followed Azazel's son deeper and deeper into the forest, the man began to fall, pounding the canopy of leaves above his head and echoing loud as thunder. japheth was out of breath when he caught up to the majestic stranger. hardly able to speak, he asked, 'What do you want of me?'<br /><br />Azazel's son did not reply but wrapped his fingers around the neck of Noah's son and squeezed until he felt the brittle bones of the throat colapse. In that moment, even before the Flood wiped out the wicked creatures of the earth, God's plan of a purified world faltered. The future of teh Nephilim race solidified, and the new world came into being.<br /><br />Semjaza's daughter stepped from the forest and placed her hands over the face of Azazel's son. She had memorized the spells her father had taught her. As she touched Azazel's son, his appearance changed"</i><br /><br />So now we know that a Nephilim was on the Ark and of course mated with his wife and so now they continue to exist. Japheths children eventually grew up and mated with children from his brothers tribe so now their is a mixture of angel blood in all the populations.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15834516550512937329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120991423?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina" href="/user/show/4272284-kristina">Kristina</a>
